Employer Refuses to Pay Wet Nurse's Wages, Wants to Sell Child as Compensation 139

Wet Nurse Sues in Court, Cries Bitterly on Stand

After Adjournment, Child Snatched Away by Employer Again

Zhang Liu, a woman from Yixing, is 31 years old. Her husband, Zhang Wanrong, has been working as a kiln worker in Nanjing. Because the family was poor and unable to make a living, Ms. Zhang came to Shanghai two years ago in November to find work. Through the introduction of her fellow villager, Tan Cai, on the third day of that month, she was recommended to the home of Zhang Qingyuan, a native of Nanxiang and owner of the Xinbao Kang and Xinbao Sheng soy sauce shops in the French Concession on Route Camille Guérin. Zhang Qingyuan, 50 years old, is quite wealthy. He has one wife and four concubines. The wife lives in Nanxiang, her hometown, managing household affairs. She has two daughters, the elder named Shengbao, 16 years old, who is already married, and the younger named Axiao, 14 years old, who studies in the countryside and helps her mother with chores. Zhang's senior concubine, Ms. Chen, is 37 years old, a local, and lives with Zhang Qingyuan in the shop. She has five daughters, two of whom have died young. There are currently three daughters, the eldest named Xianzhen, 7 years old, the second named Laipi, 5 years old, and the youngest named Xiao A'wu, who is nursed by the wet nurse Zhang Liu. When Ms. Liu started working, both parties agreed that the monthly salary would be ten yuan. Around March of last year, Ms. Liu suddenly received a letter from her husband, Zhang Wanrong, saying that he was seriously ill and asked her to go to Nanjing to take care of him. After receiving the letter, Ms. Liu asked her employer for leave to go to Nanjing. At that time, Zhang Qingyuan replied to Ms. Liu, "You can take the child with you to raise, and I will increase your salary by five yuan per month. I will send your salary to the post office every month," and so on. Since Ms. Liu had gained the trust of her employer, she gladly took the child to Nanjing to visit her husband. Unexpectedly, Ms. Liu did not receive her salary from her employer for two months after arriving in Nanjing. She sent letters urging payment, but there was no reply. Moreover, her husband's illness was lingering, and she could not leave for a while. It was not until the middle of last month that Ms. Liu took the child back to Shanghai to ask her employer, Zhang Qingyuan, for eleven months' salary, totaling one hundred and sixty-five yuan. To her surprise, Zhang Qingyuan refused to let Ms. Liu enter the door and did not mention the salary. Instead, he said to Ms. Liu, "There are too many children in my family. You might as well sell the child to compensate for your salary," and so on, treating her unreasonably in various ways. Ms. Liu, in this situation, was unfamiliar with Shanghai and had no place to live or food to eat. She then turned to others to draft a complaint and submit it to the Civil Court of the Second Special District, requesting that Zhang Qingyuan be summoned to the court for mediation and ordered to pay the owed salary. The court summoned the parties based on the complaint. Ms. Liu came to the court holding the child. To her surprise, the defendant, Zhang Qingyuan, denied that the girl Xiao A'wu was his daughter, and mediation could not be established. Now, Zhang Liu has again asked someone to draft a complaint and submit it to the Criminal Court of the Second Special District, accusing Zhang Qingyuan of abandoning his daughter, Xiao A'wu, requesting that he be investigated according to law, and attaching a civil lawsuit to seek the owed salary. The court approved the complaint. Yesterday morning, Judge Qiu Huan-ying summoned the parties in the second courtroom. First, the plaintiff, Zhang Liu, stated the details of the case. The defendant, Zhang Qingyuan, stated in his defense that the salary had been paid in full and was not in arrears. The witness, Tan Cai (the original introducer of Zhang Liu), testified in the same way as Ms. Liu. The judge then said to the defendant, "The plaintiff is a poor woman. She abandoned her own child to work as a wet nurse. This kind of blood money should be repaid according to conscience." He also instructed that the debate be concluded and that the sentence be pronounced on the 28th. Ms. Liu cried loudly upon hearing the instruction and refused to leave, claiming that she had no food or shelter in Shanghai and demanded a quick solution. She was then persuaded to leave by the bailiff, holding the child, and lingered in front of the court. Zhang Qingyuan and his concubine forcibly snatched the child from Ms. Liu's arms. Ms. Liu was alone and unable to resist, and could only watch them leave with the child.

Heavy Fog in Shanghai Yesterday 140

Since the beginning of spring, the weather in Shanghai has been unpredictable, with frequent changes in temperature. This has been especially true in recent days. During the day, the temperature on the Fahrenheit thermometer rises to between 50 and 60 degrees, and pedestrians on the road change into lighter clothing or wear camel hair. However, it is colder in the evening, only about 30 degrees. Therefore, those who are not careful when sleeping at night may suffer from colds. The day before yesterday (Sunday), the weather was sunny for a day, with a gentle breeze, reminiscent of the atmosphere of spring. Unexpectedly, by the evening, the northeast wind suddenly became fierce and strong, and the sky was covered with haze and fog. By about 3 a.m. yesterday morning, it was followed by light rain. The whole day was drizzly, and the heavy fog did not dissipate slightly. Moreover, the humidity in the room was abnormally high, quite similar to the weather during the plum rain season.

Rice and Rice Prices Rise in the City 141

Citizens' Living Standards Are Rising Again

According to the China News Agency, the National Tariff Commission announced yesterday that the cost of living index for the city last month (January) was higher than last year. The average index has been rising since March of last year. At a time when the social economy is depressed, citizens are feeling the pain. The following is a summary of the cost of living situation last month:

Cost of Living Index: The total cost of living index for the city last month was 110.4, an increase of 0.5 percent, which is an increase of 8.9 percent compared to 101.8 in the same month last year. Compared with the previous month, the clothing, food, housing, fuel, and miscellaneous categories of the index showed mixed increases and decreases, except for rent, which remained unchanged. The food category index was 90.8, an increase of 0.4 percent compared to 90.4 in the previous month. The reason for this is that rice prices have risen, and soybean oil prices have also risen with wholesale sales. The vegetable fuel index was 128.0, a sharp increase of 12.6 percent compared to 113.7 in the previous month. However, fine cloth, flower labels, and cotton thread in the clothing category all tended to be sluggish.

Rising for Months: It has been found that the total cost of living index for citizens in this city has been rising for months in the last eleven months. The total cost of living index in March of last year was 98.9, which rose to 99.0 in April. In May and June, it once fell back to 98.5, but in July, the total index was 106.9, an increase of 8.4 compared to May and June. The total index in August was 115.7, in September it was 118.1, in October it was 113.3, in November it was 108.8, in December it was 110.4, and in January of this year it was 111.0. Compared with May and June of last year, the total index increased by 3.5, which is really related to the livelihood of citizens.

Three Male and Female Guests Burned to Death in Xingxiang Genji Inn 142

A Room on the Second Floor

Opened for Less Than Three Hours

At 9:10 p.m. last night, a fire broke out on the second floor of the Xingxiang Genji Inn (a small single-bay three-story inn) at No. 7 Route Duchaillard in the French Concession. Old Woman from Yangzhou Sues Qiu Changsheng to Confirm He Is Her Biological Son 143

Qiu Doesn't Know Who Gave Birth to Me

But It Is Difficult to Acknowledge the Old Woman

Qiu Changsheng, the adopted son of the late paint tycoon Qiu Weiqing, was recently sued by Jiang Jiang, an old woman from Yangzhou, through lawyer Chen Daxun to the First Special District Court, requesting confirmation that Qiu Changsheng is her biological son and ordering him to return to his ancestral home. This case has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Peng Shi of the First Special Court continued the trial in the 14th Civil Court. Qiu Changsheng also came to the court with lawyer Tao Jiachun. According to Jiang Jiang, she is 66 years old and has had three sons. The eldest and youngest sons have died many years ago. Qiu Changsheng is her second son, born in the 30th year of Guangxu. The following year, he was introduced by the village elder Xu Zhen and fostered in the Qiu family. Now that my husband is deceased and no one is raising me, I want Qiu to return to his ancestral home. In the 21st year of the Republic, I came to Shanghai, and the defendant gave me 2,000 yuan, and so on. The defendant's lawyer then presented two pieces of evidence: (1) the license for Qiu Changsheng's adoption; (2) the receipt for 20 yuan received by Jiang Jiang in the 21st year of the Republic, stating the words "falsely claiming to be a parent and not allowed to make trouble again." The court then summoned Qiu Changsheng to the court. According to his statement, he is 32 years old, a native of Yangzhou, and lives at No. 184 Tongfu Road. He could not acknowledge the plaintiff's accusation, saying that he was adopted by the Qiu family when he was in swaddling clothes. Who gave birth to me is unknown. He had never seen the plaintiff in person. There was no contact even for family celebrations and funerals. It was difficult to acknowledge the plaintiff's claim that he was her biological son, and he presented a gift book to prove that there had been no contact. The court then summoned lawyer Wang Siji to prove that the signature on the receipt for the plaintiff's receipt of money was his signature. Judge Peng then asked the plaintiff if there were any marks on her child's body that could prove it. She replied that he was only one week old when he was fostered in the Qiu family, and she did not know if there were any marks. Judge Peng then advised the defendant to reconcile without success, and then ordered the debate to begin, and then announced the end of the debate, and scheduled the judgment to be announced on the afternoon of the 27th.

Young Woman Sues for Divorce Induced by Thumbprint, Crying Inconsolably 145

Judge Repeatedly Admonishes Both Parties to Reconcile as Before

Someone in the Audience Actually Dared to Shake Their Head as a Signal

—Shen Ruihua's Absurdity, the Judge Reprimands Severely—

Cheng Cai Gendi, a local young woman, is 21 years old, beautiful, and lost her parents when she was young. She relies on her stepmother, Wang, for a living. In the 22nd year of the Republic, she was married by a matchmaker to Cheng Xuecui (24 years old), a local man who runs the Cheng Juxing redwood dowry shop in Dong Yaojia Lane, Xiaodongmen, Nanshi. At the beginning of their marriage, the couple's feelings were still harmonious. The following year, they often quarreled over trivial family matters. Since then, the relationship between husband and wife has gradually faded, even to the point of being like strangers. Seeing this situation, Cai Gendi thought that she had met the wrong person and suddenly had thoughts of giving up on life. In December of last year,

She Attempted Suicide by Smoking Opium. Cheng Xuecui discovered it and immediately sent her to Nanyang Hospital for treatment. Later, Cheng's brother-in-law, Shen Ruihua, and others came forward to mediate. They opened a room in the Yuebin Hotel and invited Cai Gendi to come and comfort her, resulting in the writing of a divorce agreement. Cai Gendi believed that she had been fooled and hired a lawyer to file a complaint with the local court, requesting that the divorce agreement be declared invalid and requesting separate residence and a one-time payment of 3,900 yuan for living expenses, and so on. The defendant, Cheng Xuecui, also hired a lawyer to file a defense. After the court received the complaint, Judge Han Zuoti specially opened the Sixth Court at 2 p.m. yesterday to summon the parties. Both parties came to the court with their lawyers. First, the plaintiff,

Cheng Cai Gendi, stated that she is 21 years old. At the age of 19, she was married by a matchmaker to the defendant, Cheng Xuecui. After the marriage, the couple's relationship was very good in the first year. They had a daughter. In the summer of the second year, the defendant had a new love affair outside, abandoning the plaintiff unwillingly. He often stayed outside and picked quarrels at home for no reason, often resorting to violence. The plaintiff is an old-fashioned woman who only knows to follow her husband, whether he is a chicken or a dog. She has the principle of following one person to the end. Although she has been abused by the defendant in every possible way, she can only patiently endure it, waiting for the defendant to change his mind in the future,

To Reconcile as Husband and Wife. Unexpectedly, the defendant saw my concession and became more and more outrageous. Seeing this situation, I thought that my life was miserable and that I had no缘 with the defendant. Recalling that my parents had both died and that I was in such a bad environment, it would be better to die. So, in December of last year, I attempted suicide by taking opium. Unexpectedly, my family discovered it and sent me to Nanyang Hospital for treatment. After I recovered, Shen Ruihua, the defendant's brother-in-law, and others opened a room in the Yuebin Hotel to comfort me. How could I know that they had conspired in advance and asked Shen Ruihua and others to hold a blank piece of paper and ask me to put my thumbprint on it, pretending that it was a certificate from the hospital. At that time, I was too deeply poisoned,

My Mind Was Confused. It was not until the next day that I woke up and immediately argued with the defendant and others to no avail. The defendant and others' illegal behavior clearly showed that they had been planning to abandon me for a long time. I am a weak woman with no ability to support myself. I have no food, clothing, or shelter in the future. I have no choice but to ask the judge to order the forced marriage certificate to be declared invalid, and to ask the child to be raised by the Cheng family, to rent a house separately, and to pay a one-time payment of 3,900 yuan for living expenses, and so on. After the statement was completed, tears streamed down her face, and she cried inconsolably. Then, the defendant, Cheng Xuecui, stated that he is 24 years old. Regarding the plaintiff's statement,

He Denied It Flatly and said that the plaintiff had suffered from venereal sores and did not observe the way of women. I discovered it and advised her because it was a matter of face. She knew the reason and personally put her thumbprint on it, willing to divorce. The judge asked, "Has your wife studied?" He replied, "No." Cheng Cai Gendi interjected and said, "You say that I have not studied is obviously a lie." The judge did not believe it. I might as well write numbers in court. The judge agreed, so Cai Gendi wrote, "Cheng Cai Gendi, 21 years old, has suffered this injustice. Please, Judge, redress it," and so on. After reading it, the judge repeatedly admonished both parties to reconcile. However, Shen Ruihua in the audience

Shook His Head as a Signal, ordering him to oppose the reconciliation. Unexpectedly, this was seen by Judge Han, who was greatly angered. He immediately ordered the bailiff to bring Shen Ruihua to the court to be admonished. He said, "The courtroom should be orderly. You have violated the legal rules and should be handed over to the prosecutor's office for warning. Considering that you are young and ignorant, I will leniently waive the investigation. The content of this case is of great importance to you. You should quickly persuade them outside to reconcile as before. If the reconciliation fails, it will be very unfavorable to you." Shen Ruihua listened to the admonition and said yes repeatedly. At this point, the judge instructed, "This case will be re-examined and decided."

Tailors' Guild Petitions Social Affairs Bureau for Verification of New Standard Soft Rulers 151

To Facilitate Their Distribution to Members

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau is sparing no effort in promoting the new system of weights and measures, and has repeatedly conducted inspections in conjunction with the Public Security Bureau. During these inspections, it was found that Western-style tailors on Zhonghua Road, such as Fuloo Company, Zhonghua Tailor, and Guohua Tailor, were using old-system soft rulers, which were ordered to be discontinued and replaced with the municipal chi. After receiving the order, the tailors explained that they had always relied on soft rulers for tailoring Western-style clothing. Although the new system of weights and measures had been implemented for years, there were no soft rulers available for sale on the market. They had been forced to continue using the old soft rulers because Western-style clothing must be tailored according to body measurements, and rigid bamboo or wooden rulers were unsuitable for the task. Now that they had received the bureau's notification, they should immediately rectify the situation. Therefore, they reported to the Tailors' Guild, which prepared a document petitioning the Social Affairs Bureau to request the Weights and Measures Bureau to promptly issue new standard soft rulers so that they could comply with regulations and benefit their business. The Social Affairs Bureau issued a response on document number 461, stating that, following the precedent set by the bean and rice industry and the rice wine industry, the guild should manufacture a large batch of new standard soft rulers and submit them to the Municipal Weights and Measures Verification Office for certification. After certification, the guild should distribute the rulers to its members to facilitate the implementation of the new system and ensure uniformity. The request for referral was deemed unnecessary. After receiving the approval, the Tailors' Guild, noting that it was the warm spring season and there was a surge in demand for spring clothing, realized that it would be extremely difficult to operate without soft rulers. Therefore, it immediately rushed to produce dozens of new standard soft rulers. After review by the executive committee and confirmation of their accuracy, a formal request is being drafted and will be submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau along with the new rulers in the next day or two for referral to the Verification Office for certification.

Three New Titles in the Ancient Coin Series 154

Mr. Ding Fu-bao, noting the increasing number of scholars studying ancient coins, has specially published the Ancient Coin Series, selecting famous works and rubbings of previous scholars to be printed first for the reference of scholars. In addition to the previously published facsimile editions of Lü Yao Xian's Xiao Jian Four Zhu coin and Chen Shou Qing's Six Coins and Ten Cloths rubbings, there are now three new titles: (1) Facsimile edition of Zhang Shuwei's Ancient Coin Rubbings, one volume, containing many fine examples of ancient coins, all of which are difficult to obtain in modern times. Each item has Zhang's postscript, making it even more valuable. The end of the volume includes many coin molds, which are especially rare. Price: two yuan per copy. (2) Facsimile edition of Bao Zinian's Guan Gu Ge Coin Treatise. Duke Pan Wenqin said: "Mr. Zinian has the richest collection of coins, playing with them for more than forty years, so he is extremely discerning in distinguishing the origins, changes, authenticity, beauty, and ugliness. No one in the world can compare to him." His coin treatise, in two volumes, contains anecdotes and events that are sufficient for later generations to study and revise, and is not a superficial discussion of ancient times. It can be compared with Dai Wenjie's Ancient Coin Conghua and Liu Fangbo's On Coins Quatrains to form a triumvirate. Also, twenty-four items from Guan Gu Ge's Continued Collection of Manuscripts, including miscellaneous topics on coin albums, pseudo-coin albums, and mold albums, and forty-two items from the third series of manuscripts, including miscellaneous topics on coin albums, are all insights from ancient coin experts and are also published after the coin treatise. At the end is Li Zhupeng's Guan Gu Ge Continued Coin Treatise, one volume, which has precise arguments and is comparable to Bao's original work, worthy of being called a pair of luminaries of their time. Price: two yuan per copy. (3) Cai Yun's Odd Talks, six volumes. Yun was a close disciple of Mr. Qian Zhuting. This book discusses ancient coins in the most elaborate and comprehensive way. Because he was immersed in history and classics, he made extensive references, and his writing style is both elegant and informative, and his arguments are often unique. Bao Zinian once praised him as having obtained insights into archaeology, which is certainly not an exaggeration. The end includes Zhu Kebao's postscript, which also has considerable insights on knives, cloths, and ancient characters. Price: two yuan per copy. All books are sold by the Medical Bookstore at 204 Mei Bai Ge Road.

French Police Department Notifies All Police Stations to Pay Attention

Within the French Concession, poor residents who encounter the death of a child, after collecting the body, often abandon it in secluded places or by the roadside because they have no place to bury it. Yesterday morning, the Second Special Court was notified, and Judge Wang Ren, accompanied by the forensic doctor and court clerk, arrived at the office at noon. The undertaker opened the coffin lid, revealing a male child's body with its face covered in soot. The body was taken out and, after the forensic doctor's examination, it was determined that the child had died of illness. Judgment in the Case of False Imprisonment and Extortion of a Matchmaker 164

Fines Imposed Separately

Wu Shimei, an old man from Ningbo, had a son named Zuoyao, who worked on a foreign ship. In February of the previous year, his fellow villagers Chen Meilong and the woman Wang Rongshi acted as matchmakers and arranged for a Miss Wang to marry him. The betrothal gifts and jewelry totaled 86 yuan. However, his son committed a crime in April and was sentenced to seven years in prison. Recently, the woman's parents instructed the matchmaker Chen Meilong to urge Wu to proceed with the marriage, but he made excuses and delayed. Later, after the other party discovered the underlying reason, they promised the woman to someone else. Wu wanted to reclaim the betrothal gifts but was unsuccessful. He became angry with the female matchmaker and, from the afternoon of the 18th to around 2:00 AM the next morning, tricked Chen Meilong into being imprisoned in Room 23 of the Hongkou Hotel. He then instructed his fellow villagers Chen Hongyan and Yan Agen, along with the male matchmaker Wang Rongshi, to threaten him to repay double the betrothal gifts, 160 yuan. After the incident was reported, the Hongkou Police Station dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to arrest Wu and the others. Chen Meilong was then released. Wu Shimei and the others were sent to the First Special District Court. The defendant Chen Hongbing hired lawyer Fan Gang to represent him. He was instructed to await sentencing. Yesterday, Judge Wu Zehan presided over the court and sentenced Wu Shimei, Chen Hongyan, and Yan Agen to a fine of 40 yuan each, and Wang Rongshi to 20 yuan each, as a warning.

Street Vendor Violently Chops and Injures Mediator 165

Pan Guanyun Sentenced to One Year Imprisonment

Pan Guanyun, a local man, 24 years old, residing at 84 Yad Road, worked as a street vendor and was known for his violent temper. He usually associated with vagrants and was prone to fighting. Wang Caixing, a Ningbo native who lived in the Rixin Lane of Dongxihuade Road nearby, scolded Pan's cohabitating neighbor's child, which Pan found out about. At around 10:00 PM on the 14th of this month, he gathered more than ten people and went to Wang Caixing to cause trouble. Wang, seeing the aggressive situation, did not dare to resist and asked his fellow villager Wang Wenxiang to mediate. They disagreed and Pan pulled out a knife, chopping Wang Wenxiang's head in two places, causing him to fall to the ground and call for help. Chinese detective Xu Shutian heard the alarm and arrived with street police, but the group dispersed. The injured man was sent to Tongren Hospital. Xu shutian later apprehended Pan and took him to the Huishan Police Station, from which he was sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday, Judge Jiang Shuzi presided over the third criminal court for investigation. Lawyer Li Zhishan from the Public Works Department stated that the injured Wang Wenxiang had recovered slightly and was present in court to testify, while the defendant pleaded for leniency. According to Wang Wenxiang's testimony, "I was trying to persuade the defendant to be peaceful, but I didn't expect him to be so vicious. Although my head has recovered slightly, I still feel pain." According to Yue Ren Lujun Ting, "I witnessed the defendant chopping Wang Wenxiang to the ground with a knife. I was scared and ran away." Questioned about this, the defendant's testimony was evasive. Judge Jiang sentenced Pan Guanyun to one year in prison. The number of days of detention before the verdict will be used to offset the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment.

Case of Enticement and Defilement of a Maidservant Held for Sentencing 166

He Biyun, a maidservant at the Chen Mansion at 214 Shigao Tower Road, is currently 17 years old. Around September 27 of last year, Yang Yulin (25 years old, from Yangzhou), who used to work as a tea server at the Yong'an Company rooftop amusement park, colluded with the mansion's maid Xiuying to entice her out. They first had illicit relations at the Sihaijia Hotel on Tianjin Road, and then rented a small house on the Ximen Xieqiao Road and lived together like a married couple for about two weeks. Later, because Yang fell ill and ran out of money, his friend Chen Jilin (Xiuying's husband) sent her to the Rui Xiang Yuan Mao San Tangzi in Aiduya Road Dongxin Bridge to work as a prostitute. Because business was slow, the madam of the brothel Chen Guibao transferred her to a Suzhou woman Li Zhangshi at No. 3, Tongchunfang, Zhejiang Road, where she went to the Yong'an and Sincere amusement parks every night to solicit customers, leading the life of a goddess of the stage. This was investigated by the Chinese and foreign detectives of the Disuiwei Road Police Station, who arrested Yang Yulin, Li Zhangshi, and the suspect Wang Yongji from Pudong, and sent them to the First Special District Court for interrogation of the details, which has already been reported in this newspaper. He was sent to the Jiliang Institute for care. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Shuzi came to the third criminal court and questioned the defendants. Their statements were the same as in the previous court hearing, so he ordered them to be remanded separately and set a date for sentencing.

Inspection of Small Worker Crushed to Death by Elevator 167

Judge Instructs Xiangtai Foreign Firm to Provide Generous Compensation

Cao Shengkun, a 29-year-old small worker from Tongzhou at No. 121 Beijing Road, Xiangtai Foreign Firm, and Han Jinchang were dispatched to Yuanfang Foreign Firm at No. 126, Section 1, Sichuan Road at around 9:00 AM on the 23rd of this month to repair the elevator that was used to transport goods. Unexpectedly, while they were working, the elevator suddenly rose sharply, unable to be stopped, causing Cao to be crushed to death on the spot. Han escaped quickly and narrowly avoided disaster. The General Patrol Police Station was notified and ordered an investigation. The situation of Cao's body being taken to the Feilun Road Coroner's Office for inspection has already been reported in the previous Japanese newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Guo Wei, appointed by the First Special District Local Court, accompanied by forensic doctors Wei and Zhang, and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the office to inspect the body. According to the briefing from the Western Police Chief, and the statement from Han Jinchang, 37 years old, from Ningbo, residing at No. 67, Lujiazai, Pudong, working as a small worker at Xiangtai Foreign Firm, the deceased was his subordinate, and on that day they were dispatched to Yuanfang Foreign Firm to repair the elevator. Unexpectedly, while they were both working on top of the elevator, the elevator suddenly rose straight up. Seeing that things were not good, he immediately escaped from the gap, but the deceased was unable to and was crushed to death. At that time, the repairs had been completed, and the elevator had been tested twice and was working well. When the accident occurred, he immediately ordered the driver to reverse the car, but the driver suddenly escaped to the fourth floor, causing the disaster. According to Song Renlong, who had been driving the elevator for four years at Yuanfang Foreign Firm, he was following their instructions while they were repairing the machine. Later, when he drove to the fourth floor, the brakes suddenly failed, and green electricity shot out. Knowing that it was a short circuit, he escaped. According to the Englishman Coke, an engineer at Xiangtai Foreign Firm, he went to the site yesterday morning to test the elevator and found that there was no damage, but there may have been a short circuit at the time, and the driver was unable to prevent it, because there were two wires on the elevator, one for ascending and one for descending. If the ascending wire short-circuited, the machine would go straight up, and if the descending wire short-circuited, the machine would go straight down. According to the statement from the deceased's wife, Cao Gao, Guo Yu ordered the examination to find that the deceased Cao Shengkun, male, was indeed crushed to death by the elevator. The body was handed over to his wife Cao Gao, who signed and took it back for burial. The Xiangtai Foreign Firm was instructed to provide generous compensation to the deceased's family.

Young Kidnapping Victim Rescued in Shanghai Yesterday After Over a Year in Bandit Den 168

Bandits Abandoned the Girl and Fled

Handled by the Water Patrol Team

Zhang Zhilin, a resident of Wujiabao, Taizhou, is seventy years old. His son is named Daguang, and his grandson's milk name is Sanxiaoer, who is now nine years old. On November 24th of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), Zhang Zhilin's home was robbed by many bandits. During the robbery, his son Zhang Daguang resisted and was stabbed to death by the bandits. At the same time, Zhang Zhilin's grandson was kidnapped and taken away with the stolen goods, disappearing without a trace. The victim immediately reported the tragic situation to the Taizhou County Government, which ordered the arrest of the fleeing criminals. Subsequently, the county's anti-smuggling camp arrested three suspects involved in the robbery, Niu Shoupeng, Zhang Wenfeng, and Zhang Xueren. They were interrogated and found guilty, and sentenced to imprisonment. However, the kidnapped child remained missing and has not been rescued. It is now learned that Zhang Zhilin's cousin, Zhang Chunlin, through his friend Zhang Xuetang, learned that the perpetrator Zhou Changchun, along with his wife, daughter, and the young kidnapping victim, were hiding in a shack near the garbage beach in Pudong. Zhang Zhilin was immediately notified and traveled to Shanghai from his hometown by boat on the 17th day of the first month of the lunar calendar this year. He met with Zhang Xuetang and Zhang Chunlin to confirm the bandit's den and planned to report to the authorities for their arrest. Unexpectedly, Zhou Changchun learned of the leak and abandoned the kidnapping victim Sanxiaoer and his thirteen-year-old daughter Baozhen, taking the opportunity to flee without a trace. Thereupon, Zhang Zhilin's cousins Zhang Zhonglin and Zhang Chunlin, and Zhang Zhilin, went to the bandit's den again yesterday morning around eleven o'clock to monitor the young kidnapping victim and the girl Zhou Guizhen. They were spotted by the police on duty there, who stepped forward to question them. Upon learning the details of Zhang Zhilin's case, the police officer took the plaintiff Zhang Zhilin, Zhang Zhonglin, Zhang Chunlin, the kidnapped nine-year-old boy, and the thirteen-year-old daughter of the bandit, five people in total, to the team. After Zhang Zhihui, a patrol officer of the Third Division, interrogated the case, he prepared a document and sent them to the General Team for handling.

Beat Officer Saved from River 169

Cause: Soliciting Petty Bribes

Reported by Scavengers

The other night at Tanjia Bridge in Zhabei, a beat officer placed his gun and belt on the side of the bridge and jumped into the river. At that time, nearby boatmen heard the commotion and rescued him. Upon inquiry, it was learned that the officer's name was Gao Zhifang, a graduate of the police training school, who was assigned to serve at the Tanjia Bridge police substation of the Xinzha Branch Bureau. Recently, scavengers Huang Xiaolin, Tang Caiming, Tang Xiuming, Chen Laosan, Yu Taotao, Huang Minggen, Liu Mingsheng, Lu Maolang, and others filed a complaint with the Xinzha Branch Bureau, accusing the officer of forcibly soliciting petty bribes, which angered him and led him to jump into the river. After the incident, boatmen transported Officer Gao to the Tanjia Bridge police station, who transferred him to the Xinzha Branch Bureau. The scavengers Huang Xiaolin and others were also summoned. After questioning, because Huang and others firmly pointed to the officer extorting petty bribes, and it was confirmed by a number of witnesses, the case was escorted to the Shanghai Local Court for trial yesterday.

Invention of the Standard Exposure Meter 176

The key to the success or failure of photography lies in the exposure time. Photographers often fail due to incorrect exposure, resulting in monetary losses and missed opportunities. Famous photographers Lin Zecang and Gao Weixiang, in view of this, have spent years of effort inventing the "Standard Exposure Meter." It is exceptionally easy to use and can be learned in ten seconds. In just three seconds, you can get more than 130 kinds of exposure times. This invention is truly groundbreaking. Its use is based on relating the "hour of the month" to the "weather" to obtain the "total number" of various scenes and apertures for exposure time, surpassing various exposure meters in the world. Patents have been applied for in various countries. It is also heard that the "Standard Exposure Meter" can also save the "exposure time" for "motion pictures." It is ingeniously constructed and convenient to carry. It is already on sale. The list price per meter is one yuan and fifty cents, but it is currently on sale for only one yuan, plus one cent for postage. If you purchase a copy of the "Exposure Guide" with it, it will only cost an additional thirty-five cents. It is currently exclusively distributed by the China Photography Supply Company at 54 Nanjing Road, Shanghai. Wing On, Sincere, Hua Chang, Guan Long, Qi Chang, Ying Ming, and various photo studios also sell it.

The Venue for the 12th World Games, Tokyo, Is Not Optimistic 188

Italy Has Not Agreed to Concede

Finland Also Wants to Compete with Japan

Dentsu, Oslo, 24th: The Olympic Committee, which will decide whether the Olympic Games will be held in Tokyo, will meet at noon on the 25th (7:00 pm Shanghai time). Before the meeting, Italian representative Bona Kosasagito told reporters that Italy had not conceded its original proposal to hold the games in Rome in 1940. The so-called concession was Mr. Sugimura's misunderstanding of Prime Minister Mussolini's words.

Dentsu, Tokyo, 25th: The Japan Track and Field Association held its first extraordinary general meeting yesterday to discuss preparations for the Berlin Olympic Games and the holding of the 12th Games in Tokyo. It also sent a telegram to the president of the International Track and Field Association, asking him to provide great assistance for holding the 12th Games in Tokyo.

Dentsu, Tokyo, 25th: The Japan Sports Association issued the following instructions to Sugimura, who is staying in Oslo, on the 24th: "The Diet has unanimously passed the proposal for Olympic funding. The government has also stated that this is a national undertaking and will provide full assistance to achieve the goal. Various difficult conditions such as distance have also been resolved. If it is decided to hold the games in Tokyo, it will have nothing to do with the World's Fair. The Olympic Games focus on sports-related matters. A joint government-civilian national committee will be established to handle everything. In Japan, where competitive spirit is the strictest in the world, holding the Olympic Games will absolutely not be confused with the World's Fair or regarded as a side show. Please make a final effort to make this fully understood by the members of all countries." The message was signed by Ryosan Hiranuma, Vice President of the Japan Sports Association.

Japan Union News Agency, Tokyo, 25th: The International Summer Olympics Committee met at noon on the 25th in Oslo to discuss various issues and decide the venue for the 12th Games in 1940. Japan has been actively advocating for the games to be held in Tokyo for years, but Finland is also enthusiastically promoting holding them in its capital, Helsinki. Finland has the support of European countries and intends to be elected. Therefore, the realization of the Tokyo Games is not optimistic. Japan sent General Sugimura to attend to request understanding from all parties.

Progress of Compulsory Education in Guangdong Province 191

Increase in Number of Schools and Students

Subsidies for Impoverished Counties

(Guangzhou Correspondence) Guangdong Province's three-year administrative plan stipulates the steps for implementing compulsory education in the province. Under the strict supervision of the Education Department, various county and municipal governments have been working diligently. In the 21st year, the province had a total of 19,145 elementary schools with 1,110,835 students. In the 22nd year, the number of schools increased to 19,267, and the number of students increased to 1,181,968. By the 23rd year, the rate of increase in both the number of elementary schools and students was even faster. The Director of Education, Huang Linshu, believes that implementing compulsory education in impoverished counties faces financial difficulties. Therefore, he has been granted permission to allocate funds from the provincial treasury for subsidies. This year, the subsidized areas include Ganen, Changjiang, Lingshui, Lehui, Fangcheng, Lingshan, Xuwen, Fengchuan, Kaijian, Nan'ao, Fogang, Ruyuan, Wengyuan, Lianshan, Yangshan, Lianping, Heping, Fengshun, Xinfeng, and Baoan – a total of twenty counties. Furthermore, outstanding graduates from the provincial elementary school teacher training institute and the provincial normal school have been selected and sent to the subsidized counties to serve as teachers, in order to improve the quality of education.

Beiping Municipality Emphasizes Vocational Compulsory Education 192

Municipal No. 5 Middle School to Be Converted into a Vocational School

Municipal Elementary Schools to Implement Two-Shift System

(Special Dispatch from Beiping) The Beiping Municipal Education Plan for the 24th year has been drafted by the Third Section of the Social Affairs Bureau and submitted to the Municipal Government for record. Our reporter interviewed Mr. Li Jingcheng, the Section Chief of the Education Section, to inquire about the content of the plan and the increased budget. Here is a summary of Mr. Li's remarks: This year's education plan for Beiping, in addition to establishing eight new elementary schools and two kindergartens, will focus on compulsory education. However, this type of education is financially challenging, and the location is difficult to determine. Due to limitations in educational talent and funding, a two-shift system will be implemented, either by dividing classes into morning and afternoon sessions. The specific method for implementing the two-shift system has not yet been decided and will be determined during the practical implementation phase. Regarding vocational education, a decision has been made to provide full support and advance the city's vocational schools. In the coming year, in addition to enriching the content, the number of classes will also be increased. The plan to convert Municipal No. 5 Middle School into a vocational school is currently under review due to excessive costs. Women's vocational education is also urgently needed, but due to financial constraints, it will be expedited. Regarding social education, efforts are being made to promote it. The People's Amusement Park being planned in Tianqiao has not yet found a suitable location, and it will serve as a public entertainment center in the future. The Ministry of Education ordered the Opera Academy to improve its scripts and has been instructed to submit a report, which is currently under review. As for the public sports field, the engineer Guan Songcheng has completed the drawings and submitted them to the Municipal Government. The Technical Office is currently reviewing them. Once approved, construction can begin. The Sports Committee has decided to hold a primary school observation and sports meet in the spring of this year. Whether the track can be repaired in time for the first sports meet is still questionable. Supervisors are currently conducting school opening inspections for all primary and secondary schools. After completion, random tests will be scheduled to review the performance of each school. Regarding the organization of a private middle school subsidy review committee, it will be carried out on schedule. The estimated increase in this year's education budget is approximately 80,000 yuan. (Jin)

Shanghai Municipal Council Discusses Methods to Aid Students with Eye Diseases 201

The Shanghai Municipal Council's schools for Chinese children have recently sent medical specialists to investigate the physical health of students. According to the findings, four students have extremely poor eyesight and have difficulty attending classes, and 48 students also have poor eyesight and urgently need treatment. This matter has been raised for discussion by the Education Committee. The question is whether they should be suspended from school or whether other methods of assistance should be sought. It has been found that three of the four students with extremely poor eyesight have already dropped out of school. The remaining one is currently wearing glasses and showing improvement. The schools can advise parents to provide students with appropriate glasses, but this is difficult for poor families. Perhaps the Council can negotiate with reputable opticians to arrange special discounts for students who need glasses. The Education Committee believes that school medical services should be expanded as much as possible, so that students with physical defects can be assisted as much as possible. Concrete measures will be discussed further. At the same time, the Chinese members of the committee will prepare to propose methods to assist poor Chinese families in need, so that they can be discussed at the next meeting. The chairman of the committee also stated that it is not necessary to spend all of the increased revenue, as the scope of assistance should be limited to those in the most urgent need.

Shanghai Municipal Council Plans to Reform Fee Reduction for Families with Multiple Students Enrolled 204

The Shanghai Municipal Council Education Committee, considering that the council-run schools have a policy of reducing tuition fees for families with multiple students enrolled at the same time, but this may not be necessary in practice, is planning to reform the policy. According to the measures proposed by the Chief of the Finance Department: (1) This fee reduction will be completely stopped in all Chinese schools for children; (2) The increased tuition fees can be used for scholarships and other purposes to promote Chinese education; (3) The fee reduction for foreign schools will be changed to a 10% reduction for two students, a 15% reduction for three students, and a 20% reduction for four or more students; (4) The increased fees will be used for scholarships or to pay tuition fees for poor students. However, it is difficult to investigate whether the students' families are in urgent need of assistance. The committee requested the Director of Education to conduct further research and report on how to use the fees that can be increased for foreign children for scholarships and assistance, and how to investigate the students' family circumstances. At the same time, the Chinese members of the committee are preparing to propose methods to assist poor Chinese families, so that they can be discussed at the next meeting. The chairman of the committee also stated that it is not necessary to spend all of the increased revenue, as the scope of assistance should be limited to those in the most urgent need.

Scientific Research Work at Fukien Christian University 208

Fukien Christian University, a private university in Fuzhou, has been providing scientific education for many years and has a consistently excellent record. It has recently been reported that the science departments of the university are engaged in many specialized research projects, all of which have achieved satisfactory results. Here is a summary of several key points for those who care about science education:

Department of Biology: Professor Zheng Zuoxin's book "Biological Experiment Guidance," published two years ago, has been well received since it was published by the Commercial Press and included in the University Series. Professor Zheng is now also compiling a university biology textbook, and is currently organizing the manuscript. Once completed, he plans to submit it to the Commercial Press for publication again. In addition, Professor Zheng Zuoxin has also published two separate pamphlets on his research topics: "An Annotated List of Marine Fauna and Flora of Central Fujian: Amphibians" and "An Annotated List of Fujian Province." In addition, several papers have been published in newspapers and magazines, including "A Study of Metamorphosis in Frogs" and "Collaboration Issues in the Biology of Common Local Frogs."

Department of Chemistry: Professor Wang Tiaoxin of the department has been analyzing the chemistry of the Minjiang River for many years and has now reached the conclusion stage. The paper is being drafted and will be published to the scientific community soon. Professor Wang has also been specializing in food chemistry for many years. He has listed the types and amounts of vitamins in various foods that have been chemically tested. Among them, it has been discovered that the liver of locally consumed fish contains a particularly large amount of vitamins. It is said that if properly manufactured, its effectiveness is no less than that of commonly sold cod liver oil. In addition, the Department of Chemistry recently acquired a large meteorite weighing over 1,000 pounds from Minqing. It is currently placed outside the department's laboratory for students to view.

Department of Physics: The department chair, Professor Ma Chen, has been teaching at the school for many years and has rich knowledge and experience. Over the years, the department's experimental work has been based on lecture notes compiled by Professor Ma himself and distributed to students as guidance. The lecture notes have been revised many times, the content has been enriched, and the experimental methods have been improved. Professor Ma is now planning to print the book, and printing procedures are being negotiated.

It is also reported that Gan Jinghao, a top student in the Department of Chemistry at the university, was previously commissioned by the National Compilation and Translation Bureau to co-translate Julius Stieglitz's "Medicine and Chemistry" with Lin Guyin. The manuscript has now been completed and submitted for compilation. It is expected to be published in the near future for use by the domestic scientific community.

Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts and University of the Philippines Exchange Artworks 209

Communicate Chinese and Filipino Culture

The Ceremony Was Extremely Grand

(Manila Correspondence) Fine art is a means of promoting a country's culture and communicating international emotions. Although our military strength is not as good as others, our culture is developing and trending towards international dissemination. A case in point is the recent art exhibitions being held in various European countries featuring our art. Currently, the Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts is holding an art exhibition in Manila, the capital of the Philippines. The Philippine education community is very sympathetic. Yesterday, artworks were exchanged. The work representing the Academy of Fine Arts was Wang Jiyuan's "Jiangshan Misty Rain," and the work representing the University of the Philippines was the "Banana Wind Thatched Cottage Landscape" painted by Rosario, the director of the Academy of Fine Arts and a famous painter. China and the Philippines have had hundreds of years of commercial and transportation history. If artwork is exchanged, this is the first time ever. The exchange ceremony held on this day was also extremely grand. The venue was held at the Academy of Fine Arts. The Philippine side was hosted by Muke, the president of the University of the Philippines, and the Chinese side was hosted by Consul General Deng. First, the president of the University of the Philippines announced the purpose, followed by Consul General Deng's statement that Chinese and Filipino cultures should be communicated, and the promotion of culture between the two countries would follow. Then, Wang Jiyuan, the representative of the Academy of Fine Arts, presented the Chinese painting and read the congratulatory message. The Philippine side also presented the Philippine painting by Rosario, the director of the Academy of Fine Arts, and took photos to commemorate the occasion. The large-scale exhibition will be held on the 12th of this month. Personnel from the consulate and the overseas Chinese community are helping with everything. (Our newspaper's special correspondent in the Philippines, Yan Wenchun)

Good Manners Sells Well 211

Mr. Pan Dingyuan, the principal of the Municipal Xinmin Elementary School in this city, recently authored a book entitled "Good Manners." It fully describes principles of conduct, social etiquette, personal manners, and social methods. The material is highly consistent with the aims of the New Life Movement and can be used as a textbook for civics in senior elementary schools. The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education has issued a notice to all public and private elementary schools in the city that it should be purchased uniformly. It has already been adopted by 125 schools in this city, including Jingye Elementary School, Haishan, Minglun, Nanqu, Songxue, Zhangnan, Fahua, Cao Nan, and Fangde Elementary Schools. The first edition of 15,000 copies has been sold out, and a reprint is being rushed to print. The book sells for only 14 cents per copy and is distributed by the Shanghai World Publishing House on Sima Road in this city. It is also available for sale at the New Life Bookstore on Sima Road, the Ximen Dongxin Bookstore, and the Municipal Xinmin Elementary School on Datong Road in Zhabei. Discounts are available for purchases of 50 or more copies.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 212

— (Yi Qiao)

I think men are not for women and do not need to wear suits and leather shoes. At the same time, women are not for men and do not need to wear makeup. Because apart from increasing the ability of each to attract the other, I cannot find any greater benefit for men themselves in suits and leather shoes, or for women themselves in applying makeup.

The abacus is a tool for arithmetic. It is only a faithful counting device. Whether there is an error or not, the responsibility lies with the person who uses the abacus. But we are willing to be super-mathematicians and unwilling to be irresponsible abacus beads. At the very least, we must be a person who knows how to use the abacus.

Idle Chatting in the Sun about Lice 213

— Zheng Yimei

Lice, since ancient times, have been known as travelling dignitaries in books like "You Xiang Xu Jing Yu Lan", so it is clear that they are not entirely the domain of common people. Their bodies are long and oval, their mouths protrude, suitable for absorption, they have six feet, each with a claw, curved inwards, and a large abdomen, giving them the alias of "pipa insects." Wang Meng's talk of catching lice, Song Yu's ode to cooking lice, Ruan Ji's metaphor of lice in his underpants, and Jie Gong's poem of baking lice – the historical facts about lice are quite sufficient to aid people's conversations.

Catching lice and biting them with teeth is a beggar's habit. Wen Zhengming therefore has a poem about catching lice, saying: "Searching far and wide, striking with fingers and attacking with teeth." The description can be said to be exhaustive.

Lice are harmful to people, but there are also those who live because of them. During the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom era, Li Shouhui was valued by Yang Xiuqing. At that time, the examination hall collected tens of thousands of people who had shaved their heads. Xiuqing wanted to kill them all, but Shouhui knelt down and begged, saying that those who shaved their heads all suffered from sores and lice, and asked for them to be examined before execution. As a result, those who had sores and lice were spared death, saving more than ten thousand people.

Su Manshu's short notes are widely recited. He once wrote to Ya Zi mentioning lice, and it is recorded below: "Small garden with trees planted in rows, enough to wander around and admire. Sometimes I take off my clothes to look for lice and put them on the ground. A dwarf also feels around in his hair and takes out a louse, insisting that I transferred it to him. I said my louse came from my own body and is white, while your louse came from your head and is black. Why do you insist on blaming me? Although the dwarf was speechless, I am a citizen of a weak country, how can I live with dignity, how can I have peace of mind? How would Ya Zi know my sorrows and sighs?" At that time, Manshu was wandering in Japan.

Dongpo's Chanxi Collection says: "One day, Dongpo was feasting with Qin Shaoyou late at night when he suddenly got a louse on his body and said to Shaoyou, 'This is born of dirt and grease.' Shaoyou said, 'No, it is made of cotton wadding and dirty hair.' They argued for a long time without a resolution. Dongpo said, 'Tomorrow we will ask Buddha Seal. If I lose, I will host a banquet.' After the party broke up, Shaoyou secretly went to Buddha Seal's place and said to Buddha Seal, 'I just argued with Dongpo about the origin of the louse. Po said dirt and grease, and I said cotton wadding and dirty hair. When I come to ask, just say mine is true, and I will make a wonton meal for the feast.' Shaoyou secretly instructed him. Suddenly, Po arrived and instructed Buddha Seal, 'I just argued with Shaoyou about the origin of the louse. I said it was born of dirt and grease, and he said it was born of cotton wadding. When he comes, just say I am right, and I will make a cold dish meal for the feast.' After speaking, both went to question and argue. The Seal said, 'It's easy to understand, it's dirt and grease for the body and cotton wadding for the feet. First eat cold noodles, then eat wontons.' Everyone laughed loudly. This playful samadhi is delightful to read. I heard that this book is the first edition of the Zen Forest Series published in Tokyo, Japan, and there is no transmission of this book in our country.

Nine Deer Look Back 214

— Rong Yu

In my hometown—Songjiang—there is a famous ancient temple called Puzhao Temple. On the wall in front of the temple, there is a mural: "A vast plain, ten deer walking leisurely. Nine deer are looking back, gazing behind them, showing an expression of attachment; only one deer, heads high and strides forward, proceeding without any sense of trepidation." According to the elders, it is said that "this painting is a divine revelation, saying that the people of this locality are mostly attached to their homeland, with no ambition to go far, just like the deer in the picture. It is rare to find someone willing to abandon their wife and children and go to a foreign land, as rare as phoenix feathers and unicorn horns." Although this kind of talk carries some superstition and ridicule, it also has some reality. Therefore, I am reminded of the national characteristics of various places.

"Guarding their homes and not willing to take risks." This kind of disposition is not unique to us Songjiang people; people in various parts of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces also have this bad traditional concept. With a few houses at home, plus some movable and immovable property, as long as the family can make a living, they don't do anything. Sitting at home, accompanying their wives and children, and living out their lives. Therefore, I admire the people in Fujian and Guangdong, who have long sailed overseas to develop in Southeast Asia. Now, which of the islands in Southeast Asia was not conquered by our overseas Chinese? Although they are being invaded and ruled, that is a matter of national strength; the latent power is there after all. Secondly, one must praise the people of Shanxi in the past. Once a Shanxi person came of age, they abandoned their hometown and went to various places to engage in commerce. Therefore, before the establishment of banks, the major firms in various places were all opened by Shanxi people. On this point, one can also see the colors of the "Shanxi Boss."

Among the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the Ningbo people, "our fellow villagers," also occupy some influence, because they are able to leave their hometown and find a way to survive. Therefore, the strength of this ethnicity, the soundness of its economic power, and the firmness of its solidarity all depend on whether they can leave their hometown. I think if Columbus had been attached to his hometown, he would not have been able to find the New World. If Tang Xuanzang had been attached to his hometown, he would not have dared to go to India to seek scriptures. People who move forward should go out to find careers and not deeply embed the word "hometown" in their minds.

In the Vast Sea 215

— Work

Little Western Paradise 216

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 9: Unable to Compliment, Seeking Help is Reprimanded, Unable to Return Home, Following Guests with Exaggerations

As he said this, Jia Duocai rushed forward two steps, bumped Zhang Jiefu with his arm, gestured to him with his eyes, and at the same time looked around at the people in this hallway. Zhang Jiefu understood that there were too many people here, making it inconvenient to speak nonsense, so he turned his face to Yueying and said in a low voice, "Can you go and sit in Master Jia's room? If you can go, we can think of a way for you, so that your mother and daughter will not be disappointed." Yueying listened to what he said and didn't think he was just talking nonsense. Thinking about tonight, the mother and daughter had come with great expectations. Now if they went home and told their aunt that they had only come back after being scolded, not only would their aunt be anxious, but she would also laugh at them for being useless. These past few days had already been uncomfortable enough because of her aunt's cold remarks. If she didn't bring back any news tonight, there would be more cold remarks in the future. How could one live such a life? Now that someone named Zhang had come forward to invite them, saying that there was a way to think, then it wouldn't hurt to listen to his ideas. So she said to Madam Hu, "Are you willing to go back and be scolded?" Madam Hu looked at him and said, "Why would I be willing to go back and be scolded?" Yueying said, "If we go back and don't have anything to say to our aunt, our aunt will never stop nagging." Madam Hu understood his intention, and said, "Okay, okay, let's go to this gentleman's room." Jia Duocai saw that his mother and daughter were coming, so he quickly slipped away back to his room first. Zhang Jiefu thought that he was just making it inconvenient to go into the room with Madam Hu and her daughter, so he slipped away first. In fact, such things were extremely common in the Little Western Paradise Inn, so why avoid it so much. He calmly led Madam Hu and her daughter towards Jia Duocai's room. (142)

The Drifting Record of Royal Incense 217

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Fengtian, before we arrived, what a wonderful place it was to imagine! But now? We no longer feel any interest in it! If we were really forced to stay here forever, it would be the most unfortunate thing! So when we heard that person say that, we couldn't help but shudder.

One day, the Empress Dowager unexpectedly made the following statement to us:

"The day after tomorrow, we must set off to return to Beijing, because the date is already very close, and the Emperor absolutely cannot not return before the grand ceremony of worshiping the Imperial Ancestral Temple! Other things can be delayed, but this matter cannot be missed! So you must quickly prepare. — Besides, those silkworms we raise are about to start spinning silk; we naturally still have to go back and take care of them!"

This imperial decree was like pointing out a clear path for us: when we heard it, we immediately felt relieved, at least to the extent that we already knew the date of our return to Beijing. But alas! Tomorrow, the day after tomorrow, separated by no more than thirty or forty hours, but these thirty or forty hours seemed as long as thirty or forty days! The ominous feeling that we all shared, fearing that some disaster was imminent, became more and more obvious: we seemed to be racing against that imagined misfortune, not knowing whether it would catch up within these two days. Conversely, would it be too late to escape after two days? This terrifying illusion, once it entered the brain, of course prevented us from having our usual calm attitude! And the Empress Dowager, in general, seemed to have been stimulated by something and was irritable and easily angered; therefore, these two days felt especially long! (253)

Mother's Heart 218

— (Yao Yi)

She is playing with her hands and feet in my arms. Although I am so tired that my waist aches and I can hardly support myself, I am still holding her.

Her body is hot, her eyes are watery; alas, she is sick! I anxiously and constantly try to feel her forehead; ah! I am willing to work hard day and night, as long as she is not sick.

She smiles, and I smile too; she cries, and I panic; I would rather abandon everything, as long as she smiles forever!

She is gradually getting fatter and whiter, but I am getting thinner and yellower. I would rather be skin and bones, as long as she gets fatter and whiter day by day!

World News 219

— (Bing Yu)

The Smoking King of Europe: Among European countries, the country with the highest consumption of tobacco is Belgium. France and Italy have the same consumption. Italians consume half the amount of Russians and French. The Dutch and Germans consume about three times as much as the Russians and French. The Chinese consume twice as much as the Dutch, so the Chinese can be counted in second place.

The Oldest Cedar in the World: The oldest tree in the world is (1) a cedar tree in California, USA, which is now 2,500 years old, and (2) a silk cedar produced in the Indian tribes of Santa Maria in Mexico, which is already 4,000 years old. This silk cedar was just sprouting when the ancient Egyptian king hunted on the banks of the Nile. Today, it has grown to a height of 1,400 feet, making it an ancient tree unheard of in the world.

The Best-Selling Book: According to French newspapers, the best-selling book in the world last year was the Holy Bible, with a total of 10,061,740 copies sold in one year, an increase of 65,186 copies compared to the previous year. Therefore, the sales of the Bible are more welcome by the world than any other publication.

The Slaves of the World: Mrs. Simon, the U.S. Secretary of State, is the leader of the slave liberation movement. According to Mrs. Simon's investigation, the number of slaves in the world reaches 5 million. The people who sell themselves into slavery include the Liberians on the northeastern coast of South Africa, 10,000 of whom came from South America with the Americans. The next largest number is from our country.

4,000-Year-Old Skeleton: A farmer in Mezena, Italy, was plowing his land when he suddenly discovered a skeleton from 2,000 years before the birth of Christ. The skeleton was buried in a tomb 15 feet long and 10 feet wide. There were several coffins near the tomb, as well as many ancient swords made of bronze. Later, more excavations were carried out, yielding more than 50 skeletons. However, after the skeletons were taken out, they immediately turned into mud ash upon touching the air. According to the archaeologist Borgamoni's deduction, there were wounds on the skulls, which were indeed the remains of ancient soldiers.

A Strange Dissection: Since the progress of medicine, anatomy has also made amazing records. The U.S. Public Health Service, because of the indescribable mosquito infestation in Manila, had a certain anatomist dissect Manila mosquitoes under a microscope. As a result, Manila pathogens were taken from the salivary glands of the mosquitoes and used to manufacture blood serum. Injecting this blood serum into paralyzed patients can treat them.

A 7-Year-Old Academician: In Nicosia Street on the island of Savelais in Tojima, there is the son of a shoemaker who is unusually intelligent and is nicknamed "Different Interpreter." He can answer correctly in less than 30 seconds the question of how many hours have passed since his birth, and the question of how many pennies there are in 9 pounds, 13 shillings, and 7.75 pence. Therefore, he is called the 7-year-old academician.

Grains 223

Flour and Wheat Plummet in Unison

Yesterday morning, after the market opened for flour, prices for all months uniformly plummeted. Chicago quotations for foreign wheat fell by ten cents, or around eight cents, while Canadian quotations fluctuated by four cents. Based on the foreign wheat quotations, there was actually little room for significant price movement. However, after the opening prices were set, the gold price plummeted and the exchange rate soared, naturally loosening the acceptable price for current foreign wheat. The factories' orders would inevitably adhere to the environment and allow for sales. Therefore, at the opening, the current month's price only fell by one cent due to the tightness of spot goods. For deferred months, however, sentiment was very weak. New short sellers took advantage of the exchange rate and sold off in layers. Most bulls also took the opportunity to sell off their holdings, causing the market to continue its downward spiral. By the afternoon opening, as the acceptable price for foreign wheat became even more favorable, with Argentine wheat as low as $4.30, sentiment weakened further. More bulls eagerly unloaded their positions, and the continuous selling by new short sellers led to an unstoppable decline in deferred markets. In the end, the current month fell by 4.5 cents, March by 5.25 cents, April by 6.75 cents, May by 7 cents, June by 5.25 cents, and July by 4.25 cents, it is said.

Yesterday, the wheat futures market experienced a uniform and sharp decline in prices for all months during both the morning and afternoon sessions. Based on foreign wheat quotations, Chicago fell by only eight to ten cents, while Canadian quotations fluctuated by four cents. At the opening, the current month was suspended from trading due to completed delivery. The quantity delivered was estimated to be over twenty cars. Initial prices for deferred months remained stable. However, as the price of gold plummeted and the exchange rate soared, sentiment weakened. The flour market also trended downward, further exacerbating the situation. By the afternoon opening, with the loosening of the spot foreign wheat market, sellers took advantage of the situation, and bulls closed their positions at a loss. Consequently, the decline was particularly violent. As a result, March plummeted by 13 cents, and April by 16 cents. The spot wheat market situation saw a sharp drop in standard wheat prices, with asking prices also falling by five or six cents. Oil Market 227

White Tung Oil from Zhejiang is Higher than from Hankou

White tung oil from Zhejiang has traditionally been cheaper than tung oil from Hankou, allowing local firms to engage in export business.
